Closing Remarks: After the temporary motions were completed, Chairman Wu Kaixian delivered the closing remarks of the conference, saying in brief: Representatives, comrades, the Seventh Representative Conference has come to a close. Pleasant gatherings are not frequent, which increases melancholy. Recalling the conference period, we were instructed by the central representatives with earnest guidance, and pointed out the points to be worked on in the future. The representatives respectfully received the guidance with utmost sincerity, followed the instructions, and expressed their gratitude. The tasks of the Representative Conference can be briefly summarized in three points: (1) Review the work of the Municipal Party Headquarters and the government in the past year. (2) Elect candidates for the next Municipal Executive and Supervisory Committee members. (3) Determine the direction of future work, and discuss proposals. Regarding the first point, reviewing the work is indeed important. Our party advocates governing the country by the party, and all administrative implementations of the government should be in accordance with the party's will and主張. Officials, in particular, cannot deviate from the party's position and act recklessly. The municipal government and its bureaus, in their daily affairs, accept the party's doctrine and the supervision of the party headquarters. Now, they solemnly present reports to seek the understanding of all representatives of the city, which shows that the harmony between the party and the government is gratifying. The representatives have made resolutions on the reports they submitted with all their efforts, indicating the direction of administrative work in the future. As for reviewing the work of the party headquarters itself, it is even more important. If the party headquarters itself is not sound, it will be difficult to promote party rule and lead the people. The previous report and supervisory committee was elected by the Sixth Municipal Representative Conference and entrusted by the comrades of the city to plan and carry out the party affairs of the city. Over the past year, have all the measures been able to meet the expectations of the comrades of the city? This is what all the comrades of the city are concerned about. The representatives have come on behalf of the comrades of the city and should strictly review the work of the previous Executive and Supervisory Committee as the basis for reform in the next term. Therefore, the first task is indeed the key to the past and future of the city's party and government. The second point, election, is an annual event, as stipulated by the general charter. However, in recent years, new and old warlords have repeatedly rebelled, and the comrades in the rear are responsible for their duties, which depends on the loyal and sound comrades to take on the responsibilities. Otherwise, the consequences will still be unimaginable. Moreover, Shanghai is the base of imperialism and the concentration of all corrupt forces. If it is not a loyal and unyielding comrade who fights to the death with the environment, he will only be a prisoner of the environment. Now, the representatives use their twelve points of sight and brainpower to solemnly elect the candidates for the next responsible comrades from among the talented people, so that the entrustment has someone to bear. This is indeed half of the success. However, we should not take the election as the goal. Whether the people who are elected in the future can meet our expectations and not fail the trust of the comrades of the city still requires the comrades of the city to supervise them at any time, so that they can achieve full success. The third point, discussing proposals and determining the direction of future work, is also very important. What we see and hear every day is mostly dissatisfaction with the environment and a desire to reform it. However, limited by the distance between each other, we cannot gather ideas and benefit each other. Although the municipal executive committee and the district party headquarters and district branches have repeatedly made suggestions that can benefit the party and the country, they are indeed not as vivid and thorough as today's conference. This is enough to celebrate the conference. Now, each resolution will be executed separately as soon as it is sorted out. As for determining the direction of future work, it is the most important task of the conference. As the ancients said, "Nothing is said without preparation." Since we have solemnly elected the Executive and Supervisory Committee members, we should entrust them with the responsibility of promoting party affairs. As for how to promote party affairs, it depends on the planning of the representatives. Moreover, the conference is the highest authority in the city. Where the responsibility lies, we should, while reviewing the past, set the direction for the promotion of party affairs in the future, so that the next Executive and Supervisory Committee members can advance step by step and follow their own path. The long-term development of Shanghai's party affairs can be predicted.

Conference Slogans: (1) Loyal comrades unite! (2) Consolidate the foundation of our party! (3) Support our party's regime! (4) Strive for political tutelage and construction! (5) Maintain peace and unity! (6) Eliminate communist bandits! (7) Eliminate all reactionary forces! (8) Down with imperialism! (9) Long live the Kuomintang! (10) Long live the Republic of China!

Conference Declaration: On July 1, 1931, the Seventh Representative Conference of the Kuomintang Shanghai Special Municipality was held in Shanghai, and after two days of deliberation, it declared its closing. During this conference, all representatives of the conference discussed the proposals and elected the committee members with a clear mind and a fair attitude. Now, we summarize the various reports and resolutions, present the main points, and state three things as the goal for the comrades and compatriots of the city to strive for in the future. We are willing to encourage each other. (1) Our party is a political group of revolutionary people based on the Three Principles of the People. In order to realize the Three Principles of the People as soon as possible and to give the revolutionary people a place to entrust themselves, the organization of our party should strive for strictness and expansion. All revolutionary people who firmly believe in the Three Principles of the People should have ample opportunity to participate in our party, and the party headquarters at all levels should do their best to absorb outstanding members from all walks of life, so that they can be led by our party to devote themselves to the revolution. In the past, our party paid great attention to this point, but people from all walks of life seemed to lack understanding of our party. The lower-level party headquarters also seemed to lack effort in recruiting party members. Therefore, there are many revolutionary people in the private sector, but our party is sighing that it is difficult to find talents, and the progress of political tutelage and construction work is also inevitably slow. Taking Shanghai as an example, Shanghai is located in a key area, and revolutionary work is complex and requires the efforts of our party. Among the three million citizens, there are also many revolutionary people who firmly believe in the Three Principles of the People. If our party can make the greatest efforts to absorb them as party members, the revolutionary force will not be as weak as it is today, and the revolutionary work will not be as lax as it is today. Therefore, the conference believes that the comrades of our party should accelerate the pace of going deep into the private sector in the future, absorb outstanding members from all walks of life, and compatriots from all walks of life should also understand our party's position and firmly believe in our party's doctrine, such as joining our party and fighting together. It is hoped that everyone will work together and work with one heart, and the political tutelage work will not be difficult to complete, and the Three Principles of the People will not be difficult to realize. (2) The realization of the Three Principles of the People depends heavily on political tutelage work. Dr. Sun Yat-sen believed that "Chinese people have been ruled by thousands of years of autocracy and have been conquered and subjugated. Once restored, without a period of political tutelage, most people have been bound for a long time. Even if they are suddenly liberated, they do not initially understand how to act. They either stick to their old habits of abandoning responsibility, or are used by others and fall into counter-revolution without realizing it." Therefore, Dr. Sun Yat-sen advocated that the procedure for national construction should go from the military administration period to the political tutelage period and then to the constitutionalism period. During the political tutelage period, the government should send trained and tested personnel to assist the people in preparing for autonomy in various places. Preparing for autonomy is an important task during the political tutelage period. According to the central government's policies, the city's autonomy should have started to prepare early, and the district chiefs should have been selected and appointed from the trained personnel in the city. The local autonomy of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces has already started to prepare and has gradually achieved results. The conference hopes that the municipal government will quickly appoint district chiefs from the trained personnel and establish neighborhood offices within one year in accordance with Article 51 of the Municipal Organization Law, and implement the popular election of district chiefs within one year and six months. It is also hoped that the comrades of our party will follow the resolution of the Central Third Plenary Session on the political tutelage period's party affairs work plan, pay attention to the organization, publicity, and training of local autonomy, and the future of people's governance will be promising. (3) Concessions are the main base for imperialists to invade China, and they are also the source of filth and dirt in the country. They not only harm China's sovereignty, but also hinder China's development. Every Chinese citizen who breathes and lives in China wishes to recover them as soon as possible. However, in recent years, the country has been in trouble, and negotiations have been unsuccessful, resulting in empty wishes to recover them and few practical results. The imperialists have taken advantage of the situation and launched a counterattack, making a big fuss, believing that concessions cannot be easily abandoned. Recently, the Shanghai Public Concession Board hired Englishman Fei Tang from afar to study the concession issue, vainly trying to find a theoretical basis for the concession. Fei Tang's report, Volume II, even advocated that the recovery of the concession should not be within a few years, but within a few decades. When the time comes for recovery, the Chinese government should allow Chinese and foreign citizens to govern themselves and independently operate various government affairs. The Chinese government should absolutely not interfere. This kind of disguised concession system is no different from separating from the Republic of China and becoming independent. Fei Tang declared that it should continue forever. After Fei Tang's report was published, the foreigners in Shanghai told each other with color, believing that the concession system was not only required by facts, but also recognized by theory. London newspapers rushed to publish it, praising it greatly, and the concession system seemed to have gained a strong guarantee in the eyes of foreigners. Looking back at Chinese compatriots, they all seem to be indifferent. General merchants, scholars, and celebrities even take it as an honor to be appointed to the positions of the Public Concession Board, and even do not hesitate to be servile and admit that the measures they opposed to the Public Concession Board in the past were due to their position. Is it not shameful? Now, the Chinese government wants to recover the educational rights of the concession, but these people shamelessly serve on the Education Committee of the Public Concession Board, speaking for foreigners. The people of Shanghai are planning to resist the Public Concession Board with a policy of non-cooperation, but these people shamelessly take up idle positions and say yes to everything, acting as spokesmen for foreigners. "The greatest sorrow is the death of the heart, and physical death comes next." The national spirit has fallen to this point, which is very regrettable. For the sake of restoring China's sovereignty and for the sake of maintaining the dignity of compatriots, the conference hopes that the government and the people will have a fearless spirit and quickly prepare for the recovery of the concession, and use various methods of non-cooperation to strangle the imperialists to death. The conference believes that the above three matters are of great importance, so it is specially issued as a declaration, which is suspended as the goal. May our comrades and compatriots encourage each other. The Seventh Representative Conference of the Kuomintang Shanghai Special Municipality hereby declares.

Customs Ships Detained by the Navy Were Released Yesterday 106

Chen Shaokuan Has Taken a Merchant Ship to Ningbo

Guowen News Agency reports that the Ministry of the Navy ordered the Datong warship stationed in Shanghai port to detain the Jianghai Customs patrol boats. On the 30th, the warship seized four boats in the Huangpu River: Liuxing, Jinghui, Jingguang, and Jinghai. The details were published in yesterday's newspaper. However, yesterday, the First Fleet Command of the Navy stationed in Shanghai received a telegram from the Ministry of the Navy ordering the Datong warship to release the customs ships. Thereupon, the Jinghui, Jingguang, and Jinghai, the three small patrol boats anchored at the third buoy of the Huangpu River in front of the Jiangnan Shipyard, were released first at 11 AM. The Liuxing patrol boat was released at 2:20 PM. According to the First Fleet Command, the headquarters only received the telegram from the Ministry of the Navy ordering the Datong warship to release the ships. The telegram was brief and did not mention the reason. Later, reporters learned from other sources that the customs' detention of naval materials and the navy's takeover of surveying were indeed two reasons, but there were still monetary issues regarding the measurement aspect. It was said that after the abolition of the customs within 50 li, certain payments could not be allocated as before. Whether or not this is true remains to be verified. Naval Vice Admiral Chen Shaokuan took a Xinning-Shaoxing merchant ship to Ningbo at 5 PM the day before yesterday. After arriving in Ningbo, he took the Yixian warship waiting in Ningbo to Xiangshan to inspect the naval school and the torpedo source attack fleet that was in the middle of maneuvers. After the matter is completed, he will return directly to Nanjing.

Huadong News Agency reports that the Ministry of the Navy secretly telegraphed the Datong warship to detain the Jianghai Customs patrol boats the day before yesterday. Afterwards, Finance Minister Song Ziwen immediately telegraphed the Ministry of the Navy to inquire about everything. The Ministry of the Navy telegraphed the First Fleet Command stationed in Shanghai yesterday morning to release the four ships, Liuxing, etc. The Datong warship then handled the release of the four ships directly at 2 PM yesterday. Yesterday morning, Customs Superintendent Zhang Fuyun also visited Finance Minister Song Ziwen at the Ministry of Finance's office in Shanghai to discuss the matter.

Incident of Customs Vessels Being Detained 107

A Conversation with Secretary Ding of the Inspectorate General of Customs

Regarding the detention of the Jianghai Customs cruiser "Liuxing" and three smaller vessels, "Jinghai," "Jinghui," and "Jingguang," by the Navy Department's warship "Datong" at Gaochang Temple a few days ago, a reporter, recognizing the significance of this matter and the lack of detailed information, visited the Inspectorate General of Customs to investigate the truth. Mr. Ding Guitang, the Chinese Secretary of the Inspectorate, provided a general overview. According to Mr. Ding, the Inspectorate General of Customs had no prior knowledge of the naval vessel detaining customs cruisers. They had not received any orders from the Ministry of Finance, nor had they received any notification from the naval authorities. After the incident, the Customs Service specifically sent a patrol engineer to visit Chen Jiliang, the commander of the First Fleet. Chen stated that the "Datong" warship's actions were carried out under the orders of the Navy Department, but the true details were still unknown. The patrol engineer thus returned without obtaining any useful information. Now, according to the conversation between a reporter from the Guowen News Agency and Vice Minister of the Navy Chen Shaokuan, as reported in your newspaper, it is now known that the Navy Department's reasons for detaining the customs cruisers are none other than two: that the customs cruisers have infringed upon the hydrographic surveying rights and that the Navy Department's materials have been detained by Customs. However, according to what Vice Minister Chen said, this is vastly different from the facts. The Customs Service feels compelled to defend itself. It is the case that the Chinese Navy had no Hydrographic Bureau in the past, and surveys of ports along the coast were conducted by Customs to facilitate navigation. For decades, Chinese and foreign merchants have relied on this. After the establishment of the Hydrographic Bureau, key personnel in important positions were also provided by Customs. To this day, the hydrographic work of the Navy and Customs proceeds without conflict. Although, according to international practice, coastal surveying should naturally be handled by the naval authorities for the sake of national defense, the Customs Service

Page 14

has absolutely no intention of monopolizing this authority. However, the Chinese Customs has been acting in this capacity for quite some time. If the government intends to change this to be handled by the naval authorities, the Executive Yuan should order the Ministry of Finance to instruct the Customs Service to comply. Until an explicit order of transfer from the Ministry of Finance is received, the original authority of the Customs Service will naturally continue to be exercised, and there is absolutely no room for shirking or abandoning this duty. Moreover, the Customs Service is subordinate to the Ministry of Finance and is one of the administrative organs of the Chinese government. It is not a foreign organization, nor can it be considered a non-Chinese organization simply because Customs employs foreigners. The current remarks by the Vice Minister of the Navy, which clearly consider the Customs Service to be a foreign organization, are truly shocking and deeply regrettable. Furthermore, the Hydrographic Bureau also employs foreigners such as Mr. Millers. Does that mean the bureau has therefore fallen into the hands of foreigners? In addition, the "Liuxing" is a cruiser, not used for surveying. The "Liuxing"'s duties are to patrol and repair lighthouses along the coast, yet it has been detained innocently. And the three small Jianghai Customs vessels are used for anti-smuggling, yet they have also been detained. What purpose does this serve? It is truly perplexing. As for the allegation that Customs detained Navy materials, according to Customs regulations, duty-free goods can only be released with an order from the Ministry of Finance. Without a duty-free permit, Customs cannot release materials for any organization on its own, including the Headquarters of the Commander-in-Chief. The Ministry of Finance has issued repeated orders on this matter, and Customs is not intentionally making things difficult for any organization. If the Navy Department is transporting materials with a permit, Customs will release them promptly without any obstruction. Because Customs is a structured and disciplined administrative organ, it is absolutely not permissible to act outside of regulations. Moreover, the "Liuxing" cruiser was detained just as it was sailing to Wusong to repair lighthouses, before it had even set out. If the lighthouses are not repaired in the future, navigation will be obstructed, or dangers may arise. Who will bear the responsibility? As for the "Jinghai," "Jinghui," and "Jingguang," they are the only three patrol vessels in the port of Shanghai. With their sudden detention, given the prevalence of smuggling in Shanghai, each day of detention means one less day of anti-smuggling efforts. Customs revenue will also be significantly affected. These are all the harms caused by the suspension of anti-smuggling efforts. In summary, Customs is a part of the Ministry of Finance, and customs vessels are public property of the Ministry of Finance. Both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of the Navy are national administrative organs, each with its own administrative system. Even if the Ministry of the Navy is dissatisfied with Customs, or if customs cruisers have offended the Ministry of the Navy, the Ministry of the Navy can negotiate with the Ministry of Finance, which can then instruct the Inspectorate General of Customs to comply. If not, they should at least consult with the Inspectorate General of Customs beforehand. Instead, without any such communication, they suddenly dispatched troops to detain customs vessels with a single departmental order. This is a truly unexpected action, lacking satisfactory justification in terms of both public reason and law.

Telegram Requesting State Funeral for the May 3rd Martyrs 108

Guo Jingluan's Petition to Chairman Chiang

Madam Guo Jingluan, wife of Cai Gongshi, telegraphed Chairman Chiang yesterday, stating, "To Chairman Chiang of the Nanchang General Headquarters: Respectfully submitted. On June 24th, Jingluan exhumed multiple remains of my late husband, Cai Gongshi, and other martyrs in the southwest corner of the garden behind the Jiaonan Negotiation Bureau. Recalling the martyrs, I am deeply saddened. Upon close inspection of the remains, it was found that all had been burned by the Japanese, with only charred bone fragments and remnants of clothing and maps remaining. Jingluan has respectfully collected these remains of the martyrs and is sending them to the capital. I humbly request that you, Your Excellency, extend your benevolent governance to the world, with your virtue reaching far and wide, and your grace extending to the living and the dead for so long. I beseech you to remember the martyrs' modest contributions and issue a decree for a state funeral, and to send officials to first hold a memorial service at the Martyrs' Shrine to comfort their loyal souls and honor the nation. I submit this in tears, humbly requesting your compassion and instructions. Besides submitting separately, respectfully submitted, Cai Guo Jingluan, bowing."

General Lu Xiqing passed away half a year ago. Case of Western Police Officer Shooting Chinese Police Officer 110

The Municipal Government to Handle Negotiations

The Municipal Council Has Not Responded Yet

Chen Xizeng's Statement Yesterday

Regarding the case of the Western police officer shooting the Chinese police officer on Haig Road, after the Municipal Government lodged a serious protest and reserved the right to demand justice, the Municipal Council has not provided a satisfactory response. Our reporter interviewed Chen Xizeng, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, yesterday. According to Chen, this case is now entirely handled by the Municipal Government, and all evidence has been transferred. The wounded police officer, Kong Qingfeng, is still receiving treatment in the hospital, and it is still unknown whether his right arm can be saved from permanent disability. This matter concerns our national sovereignty, and all sectors should support the Municipal Government until the four objectives of punishing the perpetrator, compensation, consolation, and guarantee are achieved. Chen also stated that the incident occurred at 1:20 PM on June 24th. Upon receiving the report, the Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched the Security Team to investigate and disarmed the Western police officer and the plainclothes Chinese detectives who were with him, and took them to the Second Precinct of the Sixth District. At 3:30 PM, Martin, the Chief Inspector of the Municipal Council, visited him at the bureau. He orally presented four demands, which Martin indicated were acceptable. Around 7:00 PM, the Western police officer and others were released. Now that there are witnesses, there is absolutely no room for denial or cover-up to evade responsibility.

Opposition to the Succession of the Opium Prohibition Bureau 111

Telegrams and Letters from All Over the Country

Since the Central Opium Prohibition Committee adopted the method of "prohibition through taxation," the news has spread, and party branches, anti-drug organizations, and civil society groups from all over the country have protested, sending telegrams and letters. The secretariat of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has been receiving reports of opposition from all over the country in the past few days, like snowflakes flying. The statistics section of the association compiled the names of various opposing groups yesterday and continues to disclose them to show a glimpse of public opinion. (1) Party branches that continue to express opposition include the Tianjin Municipal Party Branch, the Yinxian County Party Branch, the Fuyang County Party Branch, the Changxing County Party Branch, the Yuqian County Party Branch, the Zhuji County Party Branch, the Jiande County Party Branch, the Yuyao County Party Branch, the Anji County Party Branch, the Fengxian County Party Branch, the Haiyan County Party Branch, the Xiaoshan County Party Branch, the Chongde County Party Branch, the Hangxian County Party Branch, the Zhenjiang District Party Branches, the Shanghai District Party Branches, the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Branch, and the Zhejiang Provincial Party Branch. All the above party branches unanimously advocated that opium prohibition should be based on the Premier's anti-drug legacy, which should not be violated under any circumstances. (2) Civil society groups that have expressed their opposition include the All-China Lawyers Association, the Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Zhejiang Journalists Association, the Hangzhou General Chamber of Commerce, the Jiaxing County Chamber of Commerce, the Hangzhou Journalists Association, the Zhenjiang Christian Association, the Guide Christian Association, and the Wujin County Congress. These groups unanimously opposed the policy of "prohibition through taxation," considering it a self-defeating measure and requesting the Central Government to rectify it according to law to appease public opinion. (3) Local Shanghai groups that have expressed opposition, in addition to 123 labor unions such as the Postal Workers' Union, include the Chinese Medical Association, the Shanghai Physicians' Association, the Shanghai YMCA, the Shanghai YWCA, the Fujian Native Place Association in Shanghai, the Huining Native Place Association, the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai, the Fujian Students Association in Shanghai, the Shanghai Daily Newspaper Association, the Shanghai Lizhi Society, the Shanghai Confucian Society, the Chinese Women's Temperance Association, the China Four Prohibitions Association, and the Shanghai All-Zhejiang Public Association. These groups all advocated that opium prohibition should adopt a policy of complete prohibition. The establishment of the Opium Prohibition Bureau is contrary to party principles and treaties, and it is a stain on the party and the country. They requested the Central Government to rectify it as soon as possible. It is reported that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce also resolved to oppose it yesterday. (4) Anti-drug groups from all over the country, including the Zhejiang Provincial Anti-Drug Association, the Hebei Provincial Anti-Drug Association, the Fuzhou National Anti-Drug Association, the Liaoning Anti-Drug Federation, the Xiamen National Anti-Drug Association, the Suzhou National Anti-Drug Association, the Taiwan Overseas Chinese Federation, the Fujian Detoxification Society, the Licheng Anti-Drug Propaganda Association, the Fengxian Anti-Drug Propaganda Association, the Yinxian Anti-Drug Propaganda Association, the Shaoxing All-Sectors Anti-Drug Movement Conference, the Yuyao All-Sectors Anti-Drug Movement Conference, the Ningbo All-Sectors Anti-Drug Movement Conference, and the Cixi All-Sectors Anti-Drug Movement Conference, all unanimously recognized that the establishment of the Opium Prohibition Bureau will render the decades of opium prohibition efforts useless. The Central Government should, based on public opinion, thoroughly prohibit it and punish those who advocate opening up opium prohibition and presiding over taxation. Their petitions are filled with tears and are truly moving. It is reported that the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association plans to collect the public opinion of hundreds of organizations and millions of people mentioned above and submit it to the Central Government for adoption.

Opposing the Erosion of Shareholders' Funds

Advocating for the Railway Ministry to Repay Debts

Sichuan Railway Company (formerly the Sichuan-Hankou Railway Company) shareholders in Shanghai, due to the urgent need to resolve the issue of Sichuan Railway shareholder funds, and the company's lack of a formal responsible person, initiated a Sichuan Railway Shareholders' Association in Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, Lu Bin was temporarily elected as chairman, and Tao Daihua was the secretary. The association will send a letter to all shareholders in Sichuan, setting a time limit to convene a shareholders' meeting to fundamentally reorganize the company. (3) Regarding the 17 million yuan owed to the company by the Ministry of Railways, the time limit has expired and it has not yet been returned. What should be advocated? It was resolved to accelerate the convening of a formal shareholders' meeting to resolve the issue. Other cases were omitted.

Advance Notice of the Cooperative Movement Lecture and Commemorative Meeting 113

Date... This Month's 4th

Address... Sichuan Road YMCA

July 4th this year is International Cooperative Day. As usual, people engaged in the cooperative movement in various countries carry out extensive publicity on International Cooperative Day and hold various grand events to celebrate. Last year, our country, due to a central government circular, held a cooperative movement publicity week for seven days throughout the country, which aroused the attention of people in society at that time. One year later, the domestic cooperative cause has gradually made progress. Last October, the Chinese Cooperative Society held its second annual meeting in Hangzhou and resolved to petition the central government to stipulate the annual Cooperative Day as a Cooperative Movement Publicity Day for continuous publicity, hoping for the development and prevalence of this cause. This year, Tong Yumin of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines made the same request. Recently, the central government has issued a circular to all levels of party branches and governments, stipulating that this day is Chinese Cooperative Movement Publicity Day. The date of International Cooperative Day is the first Saturday of July each year, which happens to be July 4th this year. The Chinese Cooperative Society, in conjunction with the Shanghai YMCA, will hold a cooperative lecture meeting at the YMCA on Sichuan Road. The time is from 3:00 PM. Mr. Wang Wuying, director of the society's publicity department and professor at the Central Political School, will speak on "The Cooperative Movement in China during the Period of Political Tutelage," and Mr. Li An, deputy director of the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry, will speak on "Examples of Production Cooperation." The society will also distribute various cooperative publications, including the "Cooperative Monthly" and "Cooperative Legislation Special Issue," which were recently published and contain the essential principles of the cooperation laws promulgated by advanced countries in the world. They are truly valuable references for the drafting of our country's cooperation law. People from all walks of life are welcome to attend the lecture. Also, the society's executive committee resolved to convene a gathering of Shanghai members on this day (July 4th) to celebrate. The time is 6:00 PM, and the location is the New World Hotel on Nanjing Road, where the society held its founding meeting in 1928. The double commemoration is sure to be a grand event.

Increased Fees and Taxes on Yangtze River Vessels 115

Foreign Merchants Suppressing Chinese Ships

Customs Increases the Burden on Shipping Companies

Cotton Yarn Freight Soars　Since the Yangtze River shipping companies have formed an alliance of six companies, foreign merchants have almost completely controlled all business-related events and price increases and decreases for fares. Although Chinese shipping companies are also members, their fleet is small and their power is weak, and they are often out of service. In reality, they are just standbys, listening to the instructions of foreign merchants. Cotton yarn exports are the largest item transported from Shanghai to the Yangtze River. The freight income is ten to four times that of ordinary goods. Therefore, foreign shipping companies compete to carry yarn, especially more fiercely than other goods. The freight for each piece of cotton yarn from Shanghai to Hankou, within 20 cubic feet, is charged at 3 taels and 6 and a half qian of silver. Yesterday, British shipping companies Jardine, Taikoo, and Japanese shipping company Nisshin, believing that foreign vessels loaded more cotton yarn than Chinese vessels, convened representatives of the six companies to a meeting at Jardine Matheson and proposed to increase the price of cotton yarn freight. In the past, one piece of 20 feet was charged, but now it is calculated as one ton of 40 feet, increasing the freight to 14 taels of silver, almost doubling the original price. This move by foreign merchants directly increases the huge income of the Yangtze River shipping companies and indirectly promotes their Shanghai-Yichang direct shipping vessels, because most of the cotton yarn goes to the upper reaches. The three foreign vessels are adding Yichang special express vessels, and this increase in the Shanghai-Hankou yarn price will make it more cost-effective for customers to reload their Yichang vessels. In effect, it will defeat the newly proposed Shanghai-Chongqing direct shipping vessels by Chinese merchants. The new freight rate has been agreed upon and will be notified to customers today. This is a fatal blow to Chinese shipping companies in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River.

Re-争论 over Deck Tonnage Tax　The Shanghai Customs has announced that it will collect a tonnage tax of one qian of customs silver per ton of goods loaded on the deck and passageways of Shanghai's Yangtze River vessels. Shanghai's China Merchants, Sanbei, Ning Shao, Zhaoxing, and other shipping companies, as well as small Yangtze River companies operating Tongyang routes, believe that the Shanghai Customs' increased collection of deck cargo tax exceeds the scope of taxation and in fact hinders navigation and destroys the shipping industry. They convened representatives from various shipping companies to discuss at the shipping association and unanimously opposed it, stating their reasons and requesting the Ministries of Finance and Transportation to order the Customs to stop collecting it. The Ministry of Transportation has now replied, stating that the collection of the deck cargo tax is a type of new tax that the Customs intends to collect, and it seems difficult to stop. However, the procedures for collection should not hinder the voyage, and the Shanghai Shipping Association should send personnel to negotiate with the Shanghai Customs on how to facilitate it. The association notified the various shipping companies to send representatives to the meeting again to continue discussing the request for exemption. At the same time, at yesterday's meeting of the six companies to increase fees, representatives from the various Chinese shipping companies raised the issue again, requesting the British and Japanese shipping companies to join in demanding that the Customs fundamentally abolish the tax on deck cargo. It is currently under discussion.

Licenses for Mid-Yangtze River Vessels　Small Yangtze River vessels, namely Tongyang route vessels, operating in Shanghai include Datong, Dada, and other companies. Their ship licenses were previously obtained from the Ministry of Transportation and Customs. However, the Jiangsu Provincial Government suddenly issued an instruction stating that Tongyang and other places are inland rivers of Jiangsu Province, and vessels operating there must obtain inland river ship licenses and pay ship license fees according to provincial government regulations. The various shipping companies in Shanghai believe that this duplicates the licenses issued by the Ministry of Transportation and Customs. Since merchant ships already pay tonnage dues, they should not be required to pay inland river ship license fees. It is inappropriate for both the province and the ministry to charge fees within the same area. They decided to petition for exemption.

Survey of the Magic Shoals Completed 116

Ganlu, Jiaori, Jingxing and Other Ships Have Departed for Shanghai

The Ri Ri News Agency reported that since the Navy Department's Hydrographic Bureau planned to survey the Magic Shoals outside the mouth of the Yangtze River, it has been actively carrying out the work with all its might. Yesterday, a reporter from this agency visited Director Wu specifically for this matter. Director Wu happened to be in Beijing on official business, so a section chief met with the reporter instead. This time, the Navy Department specifically dispatched survey ships such as Ganlu, Jiaori, and Jingxing to assist in the survey. All officers and soldiers worked very hard. All the engineering work was completed on the 30th of last month (June). The Ganlu and other ships also sailed back to Shanghai the day before yesterday.

Hurricane Signals Will Be Added to the Signal Tower 117

Can Be Completed in Two or Three Days

The Da Mei Evening News reported that the signal tower at the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Pootung in the French Concession, which displays flag signals to report tide levels and weather information to benefit navigators, has been in operation for over fifteen years. The weather station is currently repairing and painting it, and it is expected to be completed in two or three days. It is reported that hurricane signals will be added thereafter. All hurricane and storm information obtained by the Xujiahui Observatory will be displayed using internationally accepted maritime flag signals to inform ships in a timely manner.

Industrial Products Must Not Be Tested by Foreigners 118

Order of the Ministry of Industry

The Shanghai Industrial Goods Testing Institute at No. 4 Hehe Lane, Avenue Joffre, recently noted that the testing of industrial goods and raw materials has long been manipulated by foreigners, which not only spreads the secrets of our industrial technology and valuable raw materials abroad, serving as a basis for industrial competition, but also oversteps boundaries and harms national dignity. Therefore, it listed reasons for banning the practice and petitioned the Ministry of Industry to order all manufacturers across the country to ban the practice of testing industrial products by foreigners in order to uphold sovereignty. The following is an excerpt from the original order of the Ministry of Industry: (Omitted above) The points presented by Shen Xiongqing, director of the Testing Institute, are pertinent and commendable. However, it is already repeatedly ordered that industrial raw materials and goods must be tested, and the testing should be carried out by testing institutions publicly established by the state, local governments, society, or factories, to draw nationwide industrial and commercial attention. And more institutions should be established with improved equipment to build credibility and attract customers. That is why the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has established an industrial testing institute in the capital and separately informed the provincial and municipal governments of key locations, requesting them to quickly establish testing branches. It also circulated orders to major chambers of commerce, instructing all trade associations to jointly establish technical testing and research centers with similar factories to cooperate and support each other, urgently seeking to improve products and promote industrial and commercial development. Since the establishment of this Ministry, it has also continued to work towards this goal. (Omitted in the middle) And separately order the Shanghai, Hankou, Guangzhou, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Yingkou Chambers of Commerce to inform all trade associations to pay close attention to the points presented by the director and rectify past mistakes to ensure strict compliance. (Omitted below).

French Concession Issues Public Bonds Again 119

Issuance Begins Today

Principal Will Be Repaid Sequentially After Ten Years

The Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council, after issuing a public bond once this year, is now issuing the second public bond for this year, with the total amount set at 1.5 million taels, divided into 15,000 bonds, each with a face value of 100 taels, with an annual interest rate of 6%. Interest will be paid every six months, with payment dates set for August 31st and February 28th each year. The principal will be repaid starting after ten years and will be paid off in fifteen years, i.e., from August 31, 1941, to August 31, 1956, with the principal and interest being paid off together. These bonds are scheduled to be issued today.

Social Affairs Bureau Announces Statistics for Ordered Foreign Rice 120

Total of 133,350 Bags in June

Combined Total of 300,150 Bags for May and June

The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has long implemented registration for ordering foreign rice. The total quantity registered in May was 168,000 bags, as previously reported in this newspaper. Now, the bureau has announced June statistics, stating that the total amount of foreign rice ordered by Shanghai rice merchants this month is 133,350 bags. Of this, half is for the June-July period. Specifically, the June deliveries consist of 38,000 bags of Saigon rice, 26,000 bags of "Small Twist" rice, and 7,500 bags of Min Dang rice. The July deliveries consist of 24,000 bags of Saigon rice, 8,000 bags of "Small Twist" rice, 20,000 bags of Min Dang rice, and 10,000 bags of Calati rice. If May and June are combined, the total reaches 300,150 bags, of which 91,471 bags have already arrived in port.

Chen and Zhang Engagement Dispute 122

If Both Sides Knew This Would Happen, Why Agree to the Engagement in the First Place?

The engagement dispute between Chen Zheng-fan and Zhang Rui-fen was scheduled to be heard by the Special District Court at 8:00 AM yesterday. Both parties were present, but due to incomplete procedures, a second summons is required. We have obtained correspondence between lawyers Dai Ji-en and Yuan Jing-tang, as well as four letters from Ms. Zhang herself to Mr. Chen, and publish them below.

Letter from Lawyer Dai Ji-en: To Mr. Chen Zheng-fan, it is stated that my client, Zhang Ren-qing, claims to have received your letter to his daughter, Rui-fen, dated December 16, 19 (details omitted). "To alleviate the suffering of both parties and maintain the happiness of both, I have already explained the matter in detail to the introducer on the 11th, and have asked them to negotiate a dissolution of the engagement with your parents." (details omitted). My client is indeed dissatisfied with your various actions. ××× has resided in my client's home for more than a year. ××× treats my client as a hostel owner, believing that a monthly payment of eight yuan is sufficient to cover everything. It is deemed advisable to dissolve the engagement with my daughter. Furthermore, regarding your residence for thirteen months, at a monthly rent of ten yuan and food expenses of twenty yuan, totaling 390 yuan, minus the 104 yuan already paid, you still owe 286 yuan. You are required to submit the outstanding 286 yuan to our office within three days for verification and sign a document dissolving the engagement, to ensure compliance. I have been entrusted to handle this matter on their behalf. Therefore, I urge you to come to this office within three days to sign the engagement dissolution document and pay the outstanding 286 yuan. Please do not delay, to avoid litigation. Sincerely, Dai Ji-en, Lawyer, March 16, 20.

Letter from Lawyer Yuan Jing-tang: To Mr. Dai Ji-en, it is stated that my client, Mr. Chen Zheng-fan, claims to have received your letter of the 16th of this month on behalf of Zhang Ren-qing, demanding that he dissolve his engagement with Zhang's daughter, Rui-fen, and demanding repayment of 286 yuan for room and board. He finds this deeply shocking. Since Mr. Chen and Rui-fen agreed to the engagement, their affection has been profound. In September of the 18th year, Mr. and Mrs. Zhang Ren-qing invited Mr. Chen to reside in their home, providing one meal a day, with a monthly payment of eight yuan for room and board. After moving in, Mr. Chen noticed that Rui-fen, influenced by her family environment, lacked ambition, which conflicted with Mr. Chen's principles. As her fiancé, he repeatedly advised her, but Rui-fen ignored him and even worsened. Therefore, in December of last year, he wrote to Rui-fen to seek her opinion on dissolving the engagement. Rui-fen, considering their mutual affection, did not want to break up over trivial matters. They reconciled, and Mr. Chen formally retracted his previous proposal. For several months, their affection returned to its former state. Mr. Chen, considering the approaching auspicious date, actively prepared for the wedding. However, he suddenly received your letter from Mr. Zhang Ren-qing, demanding that he dissolve the engagement with Rui-fen. Both men and women have the absolute right to autonomous marriage rights, as stipulated by current laws. On what legal basis can Zhang Ren-qing demand that Mr. Chen dissolve his engagement with his adult daughter? If, unfortunately, this becomes a reality in the future, Zhang Ren-qing will be fully responsible for all the losses suffered by Mr. Chen as a result. As for the demand for repayment of 286 yuan for room and board, it is particularly base and laughable. Since both parties agreed to a monthly payment of eight yuan for room and board, all payments have been made on time, with no arrears. Now, six months after Mr. Chen moved out, Zhang Ren-qing is unreasonably demanding a large sum based on his personal opinion, which is illogical and unreasonable. The letter also contains malicious slander and reckless abuse, which are serious insults and intolerable. In addition to reserving the right to file a criminal lawsuit, I have been specially entrusted to reply. I hope you will inform your client accordingly. Sincerely, Yuan Jing-tang, Lawyer, March 28, 20.

Letter from Ms. Zhang Rui-fen: (First Letter) Mr. Zheng-fan, thank you for the portrait you gave me last time. A few days ago, I received a letter from Uncle Xing-qing. My father was very impressed with your character and learning. So, every afternoon at four o'clock this week, please come to my house, because my father wants to ask you a few questions. If you don't have time, you can come in the afternoon on Saturday or Sunday. I won't write much. I wish you well. The route is from the North Railway Station. Call a rickshaw to Gongxing Bridge on Baoxing Road. The fare is about ten cents. About twenty steps before crossing the bridge, you will see the sign of a pharmaceutical company. Rui-fen, 15th, (Received July 16, 18). (Second Letter) An esteemed Mr. Zheng-fan, I had the honor of reading your great work, and I am filled with admiration. From this, I know that you are a young man with great vision, profound knowledge, pure thoughts, and a bright future and fighting spirit. I was honored to have you visit my humble home the other day. I was surprised to read your letter of the 21st. Why are you so suspicious? It is only natural for my mother to ask about your family background and property. I am not talented, but I am very fortunate to have your attention. I am not boasting, but I am confident that I am better than others in housework, sewing, and cooking.

I specially wish you well, Rui-fen, 24th, (Received July 25, 18). (Third Letter) My beloved Zheng-fan, I have received your letter of the 16th and have been thinking about it for a day and a night. Now, I have decided to wait for you at the entrance of the Yokohama Bridge Good World at 1:00 PM this Saturday to talk. Please don't be late. Goodbye. Kiss, your sister Rui-fen, Thursday evening (Received December 19, 19). (Fourth Letter) My beloved Zheng-fan, it has been six or seven days since we parted. Why haven't you come? I know you have misunderstood something. I hope you can come to my house when you have time to talk and understand each other, so that I can feel at ease. I am afraid I will not be able to live long in this world if you treat me like this. Since you rejected me that day, I have been restless all day and cannot sleep at night. Alas, Heaven, Heaven, why don't you take my poor Rui-fen away? What is the use of staying in this world? It is better to die early and be at peace, so that people will not see a thorn in their side. Alas, Zheng-fan, Zheng-fan, I can't write any more. My heart is broken, my life is about to end. We'll talk later. Goodbye. The writing is illegible, the words are incoherent, and there are many typos. Please don't laugh. Written by the miserable Rui-fen, Wednesday evening (Received January 29, 20).

Song Yu's Rape Case 124

A Ruffian Breaks into the Room with a Weapon

Arrested by Chance Encounter on the Street and Sent to Court

Song Wen-kui, a native of Beijing, runs the Xiangji Costume Shop at 344 Guangdong Road. His family also lives in the shop. Song has a daughter named Song Yu, who is 17 years old and quite beautiful. Fan Zhao-bing, an employee, has been coveting her for a long time, but has had no opportunity. Late at night on the 11th of last month, Fan saw that everyone in the shop was asleep, so he took a pair of sharp scissors and broke into her room, intending to take liberties with her. Song Yu woke up from her sleep, and Fan immediately took out the sharp scissors to threaten her into silence. Then he raped her. Song Yu was quite intelligent. When she was being raped, she frequently hit the wall with one hand. Her father and other employees, Liu Geng-sheng and Zhou Zheng-shan, were awakened and rushed to her room. Fan escaped through the side door and disappeared. It wasn't until 7:00 PM the day before yesterday that her father bumped into him at the intersection of Xizang Road and Fuzhou Road. He quickly shouted for his arrest and took him to the police station. Yesterday, he was brought before Judge Xu of the Special District Court for questioning. Song Yu described in detail how Fan had raped her at night with a weapon. Fan confessed that he had had relations with Song Yu in April, and that it had all happened in her bedroom. He claimed he was just going to continue their pleasure that night. Police lawyer Ru Bao-yi pointed out that according to Song Yu's birth date, she was not yet 16 years old when they first had relations. This should be noted. Judge Xu then ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody, and Song Yu was sent to the forensic doctor for examination, pending further questioning.

Four Notorious Bandits from Tai Bao Ah-shu's Gang Transferred 125

Escorted by District Chief Xu Pu-cheng

After the bandit leader Tai Bao Ah-shu was brought to justice, his gang members who were arrested and are currently detained in the police station include Lu Fu-gen, Chen Ah-san, Li Wei-shi, Cao Fei-shi, and Wu Qian-shi, five men and women. The case has not yet been concluded. Yesterday morning, Judge Ge Zhi-qin of the Special District Court held a continued hearing. District Chief Xu Pu-cheng personally went to court to request their transfer to the Jiangsu Provincial Government Security Team for punishment. It has been verified that Lu Fu-gen is actually an alias for Chen Xiang, whose name is listed in the name list of the bandit gang previously seized. Li Wei-shi is actually Zhang Ai-wen, the original name in the extradition case of Li Wen-jun. Wu Qian-shi is the wife of Tang Yi-xin, who has already been executed, nicknamed "Sister Mei." In addition, Cao Fei-shi is the mother of Tai Bao Ah-shu, and Chen Ji-san is Ah-shu's younger brother. Both are important members of the bandit gang. However, police lawyer Wang Yao-tang expressed opposition to the extradition of Chen Ah-san, stating that Chen is only 13 years old and cannot be considered a member of the bandit gang. He should be released. Judge Ge then ordered Chen Ah-san to be released and temporarily detained in the police station, pending his family's return. The remaining four men and women were handed over to Xu Pu-cheng, the First District Chief of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police, to be returned for investigation.

Zhejiang Provincial Detective Team Leader Comes Too

Yuan Ting-zu Apprehended in Hotel

After Weng Jun, the Chief of the Third District of the Qingxiang Bureau in Shouchang County, Zhejiang Province, was kidnapped by bandits, his father, Weng Jin-rong, received a letter from the bandits demanding 20,000 yuan for ransom and instructing him to go to Room 304 of the Central Hotel at the intersection of Guangdong Road and Hubei Road in Shanghai to negotiate the ransom. Weng then sent Xu Gui-fang as his representative to Shanghai. When Xu arrived in Hangzhou, he reported his mission to the Provincial Public Security Bureau. Director Chen added Detective Team Leader Zhu Xiao-dong to accompany him to Shanghai. They first informed the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau and, together with detectives from the Laoza Police Station, opened Room 307 in the hotel to wait. At dusk the day before yesterday, Yuan Ting-zu, a native of Zhejiang, visited Xu Gui-fang in Room 304. After talking for a while, the detectives arrested Yuan as he left and took him to the police station. Xu testified that the conversation with Yuan was indeed about the ransom. The police chief learned that Yuan lived at 850 Dagu Road and ordered Chinese and Western detectives to rush there and arrest Yuan's wife, Chen, and Yu Quan-long. Yesterday, they were brought before Judge Xu of the Special District Court for questioning. Judge Xu ordered Yuan's wife Chen to be released on bail. Yuan Ting-zu and Yu Quan-long were remanded in custody pending further investigation and questioning.

Social Affairs Bureau Prohibits Auction of Yu Zhai Charity Property 128

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau recently received a secret report that the board of directors of the Shengshi Yu Zhai Charity was colluding with foreign merchants, claiming creditor's rights, and attempting to auction off the charity's property immediately. Increased Postal Delivery Frequency Between Shanghai and Gaoqiao 129

Municipal Ferry Offers Free Transportation

Gaoqiao City in Shanghai is a prosperous area, but mail is delivered only once a day, which is inconvenient for local residents. Since the municipal ferry began operating to Gaoqiao, the Municipal Public Utility Bureau suggested to the Shanghai Postal Administration that the number of postal deliveries to Gaoqiao be increased, with the municipal ferry providing free transportation for public convenience. It is heard that an agreement has been reached with the post office to conduct a trial period of three months, starting on July 1. The frequency of postal deliveries between Shanghai and Gaoqiao will be increased once a day, namely: (A) From Shanghai to Gaoqiao, at 7:00 AM (from October 6 to March 15 of the following year, the time will be changed to 8:00 AM) and 1:00 PM. (B) From Gaoqiao to Shanghai, at 7:30 AM (from October 6 to March 15 of the following year, the time will be changed to 8:30 AM) and 2:30 PM. Communication between Shanghai and Gaoqiao will be more convenient from now on.

American Soldier Shoots Himself 130

At 6:30 AM yesterday, a duty soldier, Belford Harold, died from a bullet wound to the head on the roof of the U.S. Marine Corps headquarters at 50 Haifang Road. His left hand was still tightly gripping a rifle. First Class Corporal Christmas, who was in charge of the radio, suddenly heard a gunshot from the roof and went to investigate. He found Belford lying in a pool of blood. The deceased was 23 years old. He had attended drill with his comrades in the morning. After the drill, he said he was going back to his room to clean his gun. As a rule, guns are not loaded with live ammunition during drill. If there is a bullet in the gun, it will fire when the gun is cleaned. Therefore, it is suspected that the deceased's death was due to suicide. The remains have been transported to the International Funeral Home and will be shipped back to the United States next month for burial.

Continued Hearing of the Qu Case 131

The American soldier who committed the crime in the Qu case continued to be tried at the U.S. Marine Corps headquarters on Haifang Road at 10:00 AM yesterday. First, the victim, Qu Shi-xiang, continued to recount everything. Then, Zhuang Lian-sheng, Wang Shu-you, and others testified. Their testimonies were the same as those of Ma Qu and others. Next, Western Detective Mooney testified that he investigated the case and arrived at the scene when a group of Chinese people were chasing the defendants, Monahan and Gines, to the back of the Gordon Road bar. The Chinese people threw stones and broke several windows of the club. Also, the chauffeur Tan Fu-lin described what he witnessed, which was largely the same as what Ma Qu and others said. He also said that Monahan and Ma Cheng-bu, as well as another person who had been stabbed, fought for two or three minutes before Monahan took out a knife and committed the crime. U.S. Marine Corps Sergeant Waller testified that after Monahan was arrested, he initially denied stabbing anyone, but later admitted to stabbing two people. The weapon used was a small knife in an ordinary pocket. He then presented the knife as evidence and said that Monahan had a wound on his leg and several other wounds on his body. The wound on his leg was obviously caused by an iron bar. First Class Duty Soldier Burt testified that two windows of the club were broken. When the questioning was over, the presiding officer announced the adjournment. The defendant Monahan will be summoned for questioning today.

Robbery in Longhua 134

Housewife's Earring Forcibly Pulled Off, Causing Blood to Gush

Wu Bao-ting, from Shengqiao, Longhua, works as a traveling salesman at a cloth shop on Yong'an Street. Wu returned home yesterday afternoon to pick up clothes, and late at night, several robbers broke into his house. They rushed into the room, and Wu was awakened and shouted. The robbers held him down on the bed and threatened him with guns, preventing him from making a noise. They broke open the leather suitcase and searched it, robbing him of more than 200 yuan, a gold bracelet, and silk and leather clothing, worth a total of five or six hundred yuan. As they were about to leave the room with the stolen goods, Wu's wife, who was a sound sleeper, was awakened by the sound of the suitcase being broken. She was also threatened by the robbers. Seeing the gold earrings Wu's wife was wearing, the robbers forcibly pulled them off, causing blood to gush from both ears. She wanted to shout, but couldn't. Wu has reported the incident to the police district for arrest.

Cigarette Exchange Industry: The Cigarette Exchange Industry Association held its first members' meeting yesterday. (1) The association's registration has been approved and a certificate has been issued. (2) Because the association's membership area is vast, branch offices have been set up in the north and south. (3) The registration certificates of the members have been ordered by the Social Bureau to be claimed. (4) The association has applied to reissue stamped licenses for concession-free cigars. (5) The industry rules were discussed, read, and passed. (6) Report on license tax matters. The association has repeatedly petitioned in Beijing to reduce the suffering of the industry, as everyone knows. Now the government has taken back the matter and appointed Director Gu to handle it. Recently, it was seen in the newspaper that the ratio was not added, and it was feared that there would be other changes in the collection. After discussion by the public, a method was decided and handed over to the executive committee for inspection and handling. (Petition submitted to the Municipal Government)

The Government's actions will bring happiness to the mall and the nation.

Various Industries Associations Request to Revise Business Tax Rates 157

The Tax Regulations Research Committee of the Shanghai Municipal Association of Various Industries recently received letters from the Shanghai Municipal Association of Department Stores, Woolen Fabric Industry, and Opticians Associations, stating that the business tax rates set by the city for these industries were quite unfair, and requested that they be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for revision. Yesterday, the association forwarded the request to the Ministry of Finance for reduction based on the circumstances. The original text of the request to the Ministry of Finance is as follows:

A request to request the business tax of department stores, woolen fabrics, eyeglasses, etc. in this city is unfair and should be reviewed and revised to meet the business situation.

It is hereby informed that the business tax rate in this city has been drafted by the Finance Bureau and approved by the State Council for submission to the Ministry of Finance. However, the business tax for all department stores, woolen fabrics, eyeglasses, etc. is still unfair. The reasons are hereby respectfully stated and submitted to the ministry for review and revision to meet the business situation.

(1) The nature of the business of department stores is completely the same as that of foreign goods industry and should not be inferior. According to the explanation of the Ministry of Finance No. 1946, whether the department stores in the large commercial ports are under the scope of foreign goods industry should be clearly defined. According to the nature of the department store, it is an expansion of foreign goods business and should be temporarily levied business tax as foreign goods industry. It is very clear that the draft proposed by the city for the foreign goods industry is levied at a rate of 2 per 1,000, while the department stores with the same nature are levied at a rate of 3 per 1,000. This is not only unfair, but also violates the interpretation of the Ministry of Finance.

(2) Woolen fabrics, foreign fabrics, silk and satin, are all the raw materials for clothing, and most of them are operated in the same stores. The tax rates set in the draft are 1 per 1,000 for cotton fabrics and silk fabrics, and 3 per 1,000 for the woolen fabrics industry. Although most woolen fabrics are imported, it is not appropriate to levy a high tax rate on the domestic woolen fabrics industry at this time. Moreover, Article 7 of the Supplementary Measures to the Levy Tax stipulates that foreign goods and native goods shall be taxed at the same tax rate. The ministry should reduce the business tax of the woolen fabrics industry to the same rate of 1 per 1,000 as the cotton fabrics and silk fabrics industries.

(3) Eyeglasses are tools for eye protection. Many countries in the world list them as medicinal materials and supplies. However, the draft proposed by the city imposes the highest tax rate, as if they were luxury goods, which is not a fair approach. The ministry should reduce the business tax of the eyeglasses industry to the same rate of 1 per 1,000 as the medicinal materials industry.

The request has been sent to the association by the industries, and it is necessary to forward it. When the city's business tax is revised, the department stores should be taxed at the same rate of 2 per 1,000 as the foreign goods industry, and the woolen fabrics industry should be taxed at the same rate as the cotton fabrics industry, silk fabrics industry, and the eyeglasses industry should be taxed at the same rate as the medicinal materials industry at 1 per 1,000 to show fairness and conform to the business situation.

Laborers of the French Municipal Council Demand Improved Treatment 158

Yesterday morning around 7:00 AM, all the laborers of the French Municipal Council, dissatisfied with the Western factory director "Leng Dong" (transliteration), unanimously went on strike in all departments. They sent representatives with a petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Bureau, requesting assistance and urging all labor circles to provide practical support. The demands for improved treatment put forward by all laborers are as follows: (1) The factory director's abuse of workers should result in dismissal. (2) The French Municipal Council Workers' Union should be recognized and given a monthly subsidy of 500 taels of silver. (3) Double salary for one month's wages should be given at the end of the year. (4) Chinese and foreign holidays should be uniformly observed with rest; those who work should receive double salary. (5) Workers' working hours should be 8 hours per day, and staff working hours should be 6 hours per day; overtime should be calculated according to the wages earned; Saturday afternoons should be off. (6) Wages should be increased by 20% uniformly each year. (7) Wages not increased last year should be supplemented uniformly, and rice subsidies should be supplemented in the same way. (8) Each tael of wage should be calculated at 1.4 yuan in silver dollars and should not be changed. (9) One month of leave should be given uniformly each year, without deducting wages. (10) The minimum salary for staff should be 50 taels of silver per person, and the minimum salary for workers should be 30 taels of silver; inspectors should receive a monthly allowance of 15 yuan for Shanghai horse fees. (11) Workers should be allowed sick leave without deduction of wages. (12) Fines should not be forcibly deducted for minor reasons, and staff and workers should not be dismissed without cause; if dismissed, they should be given five years' worth of severance pay. (13) Staff and workers who have worked for one year should be given two months' worth of retirement pay upon retirement, and more will be given by analogy. (14) Temporary workers should be calculated according to the standards of permanent workers, and their wages and treatment should be the same as permanent workers. (15) Workers who have been dismissed from the union without cause should be reinstated, and their wages should be supplemented. (16) There should be no restrictions on the number of workers or the time limit for work. (17) Workers' wages should be doubled on snowy days in cold weather.

Publication of the Administrative Management Reality Compiled by the Municipal Public Works Bureau 160

The Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau is trying to use scientific methods to carry out administration. Chinese and foreign people who go to visit see its complete internal layout and the meticulousness of its handling procedures, and all praise it. Recently, the bureau, in view of the fact that outsiders often request regulations, charts, and management methods, numbering several times a day, and being overwhelmed, has compiled a systematic report called "The Reality of Administrative Management of the Shanghai Municipal Public Works Bureau." It details the organization of the agency, the handling of official documents, the compilation and management of archives, the handling of official duties and attendance, the collection and storage of books, as well as monetary accounting, material accounting, general affairs personnel, etc., from the initial situation, through various changes, to the present state. It is said that the book is printed by the Shanghai Dadongmen Jiaotong Printing House, and has been published. The text is about 300,000 words, with more than 100 charts. The whole book is printed in No. 4 font on high-quality Chinese Lian Shi paper. The actual price of each book is two yuan in national currency, and official agencies only pay half price, one yuan, when purchasing with a formal letter.

Letter 162

To the Editor,

I have just read a special dispatch in today's issue of your newspaper regarding the estimated income from the opium suppression policy. The Nanjing dispatch stated that the Anti-Opium Association's investigation revealed that there are at least five million opium addicts in China today, and that the number of people using substitutes in Shanxi, Shaanxi, Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Rehe actually exceeds five million. If each person pays an opium tax of 20 yuan per year, that would be a revenue of 20 million, enough to cover half of China's total military expenditure.

We have absolutely never made such a statement, and anti-opium organizations throughout the country would absolutely not make such a proposal. As for Nanjing, there is currently no anti-opium organization established there. We do not know the basis for this news. Our association has always advocated a policy of complete suppression and prohibition, and opposes collecting opium taxes to fund military and administrative expenses. Our position on opium suppression is based entirely on the late Dr. Sun Yat-sen's anti-opium teachings. We would never consider taxing opium under any circumstances. This dispatch is simply untrue and can easily cause misunderstandings.

Therefore, we respectfully request that your newspaper promptly correct this to clarify the truth, and please publish the original letter as is. We would be most grateful.

Sincerely,

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Association

July 2nd

To the Editor,

I have just received a statement from my client, Tang Genquan, stating that he read a news item in today's local newspapers about a bloody incident at the Huayanglou on Fuyou Road, implicating Genquan and others who fled to avoid involvement. This is not in accordance with the facts. Genquan was a detective in the Public Security Bureau, stationed in a district, and has always been careful and dutiful, with no misconduct. He does not know the "Little Wang" mentioned in the report, and he was not at the Huayanglou at the time of the incident. Since the incident had nothing to do with Genquan, why would he need to avoid involvement? The Second Precinct of the First District has also not investigated him. The report in the newspapers is clearly not factual and is likely to damage his reputation. He has entrusted me to write a letter to request a correction.

Therefore, I am writing to you respectfully to ask for a correction, as a matter of public interest.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Huang Qiying

July 2nd, 20th Year

Financial Banks Still Closed 163

Financial Market Sluggish

Yesterday, banks remained closed, and the market was dull and uninteresting. The prices of foreign silver dollars in the market were also very depressed. The opening price in the morning was 7 qian, 2 fen, 6 li, 5 hao, and the closing price in the afternoon was 7 qian, 2 fen, 6 li, a slight decrease of 2 hao and 5 si compared to the previous day. The silver swap rate, however, felt higher. The morning rate was 1 qian, and the afternoon rate was 1 qian and 4 fen, due to the lack of activity in the head lining during the closure. The transaction volume for export payments was 260,000 in the morning and 715,000 in the afternoon. The transaction volume for banknotes was only 25,000 in the afternoon. The over-the-counter banknote transaction volume was 65,000 in the morning and 50,000 in the afternoon. Qianzhuang cleared over 3.8 million in foreign public bills and over 37 million in silver public bills. Remittances from various routes amounted to over 400,000. Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market Still Circulating 165

The yarn market trend is very weak, but the overseas cotton yarn situation is still firm. However, local sentiment has softened, as large households have sold, and the amount is very large, so the market atmosphere has become very loose, and retail bulls are even more panic-stricken, so the market is difficult to stabilize. As for the sellers, seeing that a certain large household has the intention of giving up, they are more courageous and throw out all together when prices rise, so the market is even weaker. However, 16-count and 20-count yarn prices are very tight, and Japanese yarn prices are rising, but coarse yarn trends are more stagnant and deeply affected. The internal situation of futures yarn is complicated, so the spot price is rising, but the standard yarn is falling, all in a confusing situation.

Grain and Rice Market Rises and Then Loosens 168

Xinzha Yesterday, about twenty or thirty boats arrived at the Western Road from various gangs. Sales were initially sluggish and then brisk. Su Chang thick japonica rice was extremely sluggish in the morning, and prices continued to soften. Store intentions turned weak, and top goods continued to be weak by 2 jiao. Middle customs, on the other hand, felt slightly stronger, but this was not a formal market. Thin rice arrived in abundance but sales were weak, and the market softened again by 2 or 3 chi. Du Yang tip was still actively inquired about on this street, and the source was not very abundant, so prices dropped nearly a chi. Ba Bu tip sales were poor and the goods were limited. Sentiment was not good, so the trend fell by about 1 jiao. Few guest tips were loaded, and the sales were few, so the price recovered by 1 or 2 jiao. The large plate of glutinous rice also went downstream. All rice in the city was uniformly tired. The opening of river goods was less than 2,000 shi.

Hunan Yesterday's rice situation was sunny, with 32 or 33 ships arriving. Urban and rural sales markets were sluggish. Early rice was still arriving sporadically. The arrival of early rice from Su, Xi, and Su, and other goods was quite frequent, but buying sentiment was quiet, and the market was therefore tired. The large plate shortened by 3 or 4 jiao. The transactions of Nan Gang's various thin rice from this street and rural gangs were extremely sluggish, so they shortened by 2 or 3 jiao. Du Yang tip was still considered acceptable for fresh tops, but the secondary tops were sluggish, and the price shortened by nearly a chi. Shadowed, high-quality goods remained fixed, while mid-range goods were cheapened and cornered. Sales of foreign rice were not smooth, and rural stomachs were also watching, so prices continued to be down a small jiao or so.

Flour Market Initially Tired and Then Strong 169

Yesterday's flour market showed signs of initial fatigue followed by strength in various months after the opening. Because the Chicago foreign report price was about 5 or 7 jiao lower, the market atmosphere was once weak. However, because the factory throwing was very quiet, and because the negotiations between the United States and France had not yet been properly completed, there was a deep fear that the gold market opening price would have at least one impact. As a result, the sentiment remained strong, and the throwers suddenly hesitated. Until the afternoon opening, because the manufacturers still tended to reject the situation, the sentiment of outsiders was even more energetic. In addition, although Tianjin's current sales were not smooth, those who wanted to do futures were quite abundant, so the market presented a strong step again. However, when the country is still in a state of surplus, if the foreigners stubbornly raise the price too much, it is difficult to avoid the throwing pressure of foreign wheat. As a result, this month was good for five li, August was good for one fen, September and October were good for seven and a half li, and November and December were good for one fen.

Wheat Market Difficult to Get Too Good 170

Yesterday's wheat futures market, after the opening of the afternoon market in various months, was initially settled due to the foreign wheat report being 5 or 7 jiao lower. However, after that, outsiders competed to cover their short positions, and the sentiment was stimulated. Although there was no market for gold prices, the opinions on the US-French war debt had not yet been approached, and speculators were also very active in preventing changes in the gold market. On average, each month was compared and calculated to recover 4 or 5 fen. Until the various plates in the afternoon, the accumulation of spot wheat was very abundant after all, and the manufacturers were indifferent and had no large-scale appetite. In this case, it was impossible to be too high (factory and merchant households had eight ships of foreign wheat in the opening price, and if this batch was transferred, people's hearts might have to change drastically), so the selling atmosphere was strong, and the market returned to a small two or three fen. After observing, because of the abundant existence of spot wheat, it is still not optimistic. As a result, July, August and September were better than one fen, October and November were better than three fen, and December was incomparable. The situation of spot wheat is still softening. The manufacturers had too thick a reserve, so they had to respond. The whole city opened 4,000 bags of Taizhou Taipingqiao Huangqiaokou Anqing Chuzhou Nanjing Liuhe Wusong Anting Penglai wheat, which was handled by Fuxin Shenda.

Yushan Zi Tea High Price and Slow Sales 174

This year's spring tea production in Yu County has been reduced. Most of it is supplied to domestic shops and stores. The tea shops in Hekou Zhangcun Street Shangrao Foreign Village also have a considerable sales market. The remaining spring tea is scarce. Recently, the Zi tea in the county is also being picked. The out-of-stock is better than the first tea. And because the weather is balanced, the production is still abundant. However, because this year's tea shortage has been reported from all roads, the quality and taste of the Zi tea is excellent, so everyone lives for the odd goods. The market price has been raised to 70 yuan per dan. Although the Anhui and Ben bang tea dealers have been pouring in to talk about the market, they are afraid to open the scale and buy because of the high disk price, and the sales market is therefore slow.

Shanghai Market

Market News 189

The Construction Book Bureau, located at the west end of Nanyang Bridge, announces that it has been entrusted by a northern straw hat factory with the latest styles of high-quality gentleman's straw hats, both soft and hard, which are not available in Shanghai. The price ranges from three yuan to five yuan per hat. The stock is limited. Anyone interested in summer fashion is welcome to come and take a look.

The Xiangzu Calligraphy and Painting Society, located at No. 10 Shude South Lane, at the intersection of Beile Road and Wangzhi Road, announces that the society's fan exhibition opened yesterday and was unusually popular with visitors. More than a thousand pieces of artwork have been sold, and the exhibition has been extended for three days.

Theater News 190

The Empire Theater announces that the eighteen-part film "Burning of the Red Lotus Monastery" narrates the plans of the Kunlun and Kongtong sects to set up a net of heaven and earth. The characters of the two sects display their wisdom and exhaust their magic. The scenes are extremely intense, especially the scene of the Golden Arhat angrily fighting the giant monster, where jade and stone are burned together, which is even more exciting. This film will be shown at the theater today, along with a film of the truth about the Shaanxi disaster.

Publishing News 191

The Qingbai Over Weekly Society announces that the journal is organized by emerging young writers with the aim of elucidating the frank thoughts of young people. The inaugural issue is scheduled to be published on July 4th. Submissions of articles criticizing social phenomena, recording special aspects of life, as well as novels, poems, school news, etc., are all welcome. Once published, generous compensation will be given. The society's address is No. 5 Heng Deli, Jiucang Street, Laobeimen.
